  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9c530528-6e29-4925-83cb-235db71fd59d'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText1357462010003113321" style="display:none">Juliet Young always writes letters to her mother, a world-traveling photojournalist. Even after her mother's death, she leaves letters at her grave. It's the only way Juliet can cope.<br /><br />Declan Murphy isn't the sort of guy you want to cross. In the midst of his court-ordered community service at the local cemetery, he's trying to escape the demons of his past.<br /><br />When Declan reads a haunting letter left beside a grave, he can't resist writing back. Soon, he's opening up to a perfect stranger, and their connection is immediate. But neither Declan nor Juliet knows that they're not actually strangers. When life at school interferes with their secret life of letters, sparks will fly as Juliet and Declan discover truths that might tear them apart.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4557389926524176640">Reread!<br/>Beautiful! Just beautiful! <br/><br/>I love that it is not just a love-story. There's so much more to it. It's so much deeper. <br/>The tone of the book is heavy. Its pages are filled with grief and anger and misunderstandings. It was intense to read and a lot to take in because the burden that weighed so heavily on our main characters weighed on me. <br/><br/>I could’ve read many more pages. I never wanted their story to end. They found each in the midst of absolute despair and clung to the understanding they fo</span>
  <span id="freeText4557389926524176640" style="display:none">Reread!<br />Beautiful! Just beautiful! <br /><br />I love that it is not just a love-story. There's so much more to it. It's so much deeper. <br />The tone of the book is heavy. Its pages are filled with grief and anger and misunderstandings. It was intense to read and a lot to take in because the burden that weighed so heavily on our main characters weighed on me. <br /><br />I could’ve read many more pages. I never wanted their story to end. They found each in the midst of absolute despair and clung to the understanding they found in one another, because so much of that was missing from their lives. They weren't perfect, but they didn't need to be.<br />Who they were was enough.<br /><br />I loved it!</span>

<div id="review_1864335380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864335380" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864335380?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408883525" href="/book/show/33857632-letters-to-the-lost">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864335380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1531505678682680509"><b>REREAD #2: July 2018</b><br/><br/>Brb, just <i>sobbing</i>. <b>I can't even say how powerful, how meaningful, and how emotional this book is.</b> It seriously has STOLEN my heart and if I can ever write contemporaries half as good as this afjkdlsad I will die happy. And can I just say the audiobook is fantastic?? The voice actors put so much passion into it....the whole thing was just incredible.<br/><br/><b>MOMENTS:</b><br/>☆ Declan breaking down in tears just asking and asking to be loved<br/>☆ every time they talked about snap-judgements, and how</span>
  <span id="freeText1531505678682680509" style="display:none"><b>REREAD #2: July 2018</b><br /><br />Brb, just <i>sobbing</i>. <b>I can't even say how powerful, how meaningful, and how emotional this book is.</b> It seriously has STOLEN my heart and if I can ever write contemporaries half as good as this afjkdlsad I will die happy. And can I just say the audiobook is fantastic?? The voice actors put so much passion into it....the whole thing was just incredible.<br /><br /><b>MOMENTS:</b><br />☆ Declan breaking down in tears just asking and asking to be loved<br />☆ every time they talked about snap-judgements, and how that's <i>one photograph</i> of a person's life and how dare you judge them all on one photograph<br />☆ Juliet pulling herself up for her problematic behaviour<br />☆ Juliet grieving so realistically and heartbreakingly<br />☆ I FELT EVERY WORD OF THIS BOOK<br />☆ All the adults that didn't give up on these kids. ALL of them. The teachers, Juliet's dad, Rev's parents...<br />☆ REV REVVVVVV I am about to start his book now ajfdlksad<br />☆ Literally one of my <b>favourite contemporaries of all time</b> I just can't even<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>READ #1: May 2017</b><br /><b>Oh this was a pocketful of heartbreaking and heartwarming surprises.</b> I really loved the author's other book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23454468.Thicker_Than_Water" title="Thicker Than Water by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Thicker Than Water</a>, but I didn't expect to fall sooooo wholly in love with Letters To the Lost. PEOPLES, THIS BOOK IS PHENOMENAL. It's sad and it's sweet and the characters were so dimensional and complex and real. It was also DARN INCONVENIENT because I didn't want to put it down. The pages just flew past, with me feeling <i>all the things</i> which seems like a health hazard to my emotions.<br /><br />There there, Cait, CALM DOWN IT'LL BE OKAY HAVE A CRUMPET.<br /><br /><b>L I K E S</b><br />• <b>It features letters and FRIENDSHIP!</b> Obviously. But more importantly is the anonymous friendships...and while these two knew that they went to the same school/were same age (after a few back and forths), their relationship was still kind of like what one has with an internet friend. And I LOVED THAT. They got to know the deep and venerable sides of each other. They weren't hindered by pre-conceived prejudice or judgement. It was so simple and pure and sweet. Until obviously it gets ALL MESSY and aghhhh. My bleeding heart. <b>Also the book is not TOLD in letters. There's just a letter at the front of each chapter.</b><br /><b> • But seriously, the FRIENDSHIP.</b> Even while Declan and Juliet are anonymously becoming friends, they also both have epic BFFs that I just want to kidnap and adopt immediately. Declan's best friend, Rev, comes from an abused home and is now adopted but he has a bucket load of PTSD...and he's also the sweetest kindest boy who is THERE for Declan. And Juliet has this epic friend of Rowan who doesn't let her have panic attacks alone and will forcibly pull her out of depressive episodes with Mexican food and hugs. <b>Just the emphasis on GOOD and healthy friendships in here alone makes the book so perfect.</b><br /><b> • It's quite sad though, with both Declan and Juliet suffering from a lot of grief.</b> Juliet's grief at losing her mother makes her quite nasty on occasion, but in a "righteous" way which I found SO annoying. But then there was character development!! GLORIOUS CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT. And Declan is aggressive and puts on all the "bad delinquent boy" vibes with his criminal record and his terrible attitude at school. <b>But inside they're both breaking apart with grief, blame, and anxiety.</b> I can't even express how well it was written and how I loved them both. They're intensely flawed characters, and they grow so so much throughout the book.<br /><b> • Also I loved how it didn't feature romance!</b> The cliche route would be to make them fall in love over letters, right? WELL KIND OF, BUT ALSO NOT QUITE. First they became friends. First they focus on themselves. Dealing with things. Confronting themselves. THEN THEY ADMIT THEY AHVE A CRUSH AND AJFDKSLAD IT'S SO CUTE. I ABSOLUTELY SHIP IT.<br /><b> • Also the messages about "no one is everything they seem" are intensely important.</b> Look we all show the world what we want to. And we get judged for it. And just the quips and call outs of this were so <i>on point</i>...I can't even. I'm so impressed. Like when Juliet is really unnecessarily cruel to Declan (whom she doesn't know is her anonymous writing buddy) at school, she later gets called out for it with the thought of: just because someone is "known" to be a delinquent, does that mean they deserve your cruelty?? You never never never know the whole story so DON'T treat people like you do.<br />• <b>ALSO I LOVE DECLAN.</b> Angry sad broken fragile child. &lt;3 His home life sucks, he doesn't feel loved or feel he <i>deserves</i> to be loved. His dad's in prison and his sister is dead and he blames himself. AND LITERALLY EVERYONE HATES HIM WITHOUT EVEN BOTHERING TO KNOW HIM. (Except Rev whom I adore.) No no, it's ok, I'm not having an emotion here.<br /><b> • And there's quite a lot of car stuff!</b> And by the way I just said "car stuff" you know I haven't got a CLUE about the difference between a carburetor and carp fish. But yet!! I appreciated it! It features lots of breaking down cars and Declan fixing cars because he's #fab.<br /><b> • Also it features photography!</b> I love photography!! I may only use automatic on my dslr, shhhh, but I still loved reading about it.<br /><b> • ALSO THE WRITING IS JUST EXQUISITE.</b> Did I mention I was glued to the page?!??? And how <i>real</i> and <i>complex</i> all the characters were? It's an intense sign of good writing when you want to read spin-offs about the secondary characters (I WANT A REV BOOOK) and when you also don't want it to end because you're in love with Declan and Juliet. The pacing was A+ and the emotion was just so beautifully crafted the whole time. EMOOOOOTION. Feel all the things.<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: Basically I'm just going to gush my liver out here proclaiming how good this book is.</b> It totally took me by surprise, but I <i>adore</i> it. Heartfelt and tragic and bittersweet and also <i>hopeful</i>. Ugh words. I have none. Just go read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1531505678682680509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2081453721" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081453721" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2081453721?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sana by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/49148508-may">may ❀</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=im-all-kinds-of-shook">im-all-kinds-of-shook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=bf">bf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2081453721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1757322429806828589">When I first saw this book I thought it would be a dumb, cheesy, and extra adorable cute contemporary with some like, forbidden romance or some shit that would make you sob your heart out for the characters (I DON'T READ BLURBS LMAO OK) and I avoided it for months. Since this was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>may's</a> favorite sappy contemporary, I ASSUMED it would be what I described. OH HOW WRONG I WAS SOMEONE FEEL FREE TO PUNCH ME IN THE FACE!!<br/><br/>What I got was a book about <b>labels, judgement, grief, love, acceptance, friendship</b></span>
  <span id="freeText1757322429806828589" style="display:none">When I first saw this book I thought it would be a dumb, cheesy, and extra adorable cute contemporary with some like, forbidden romance or some shit that would make you sob your heart out for the characters (I DON'T READ BLURBS LMAO OK) and I avoided it for months. Since this was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">may's</a> favorite sappy contemporary, I ASSUMED it would be what I described. OH HOW WRONG I WAS SOMEONE FEEL FREE TO PUNCH ME IN THE FACE!!<br /><br />What I got was a book about <b>labels, judgement, grief, love, acceptance, friendship and moving on.</b> It's so deep and moving, it made my stone cold (love you Demi!!!) heart <i>melt</i> I was a sobbing mess, I literally still cannot form coherent sentences and find accurate emotions to describe what the fuck I'm feeling. <br /><br />Actually I lied. What I'm still feeling right now is:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>ADKNSAJKFBSDJKAGVBASDFKLblfbqlgbrilqefkl;bneriqbnSKFHDKGKGNEFKLGNFFUKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUCKFUFKCUFKCUCF</i>
</b><br /><br />What I loved most about this book is that our two character's didn't need love, sex or romance to help them move on and feel better. They wrote letters to each other about their grief, their struggles, about how no one understands and talking about it to each other and sharing their grief helped them so so much, it's fucking real!!!! <br /><br />It's such an emotional book that handles such a sad topic and throughout the book I was just...my eyes were just sweating so much phew boy was it fucking melting hot that day!!!!<br /><br />Okay seriously, this book is emotional torture because what they talk about is just so deep, sad, but so so inspiring. This book is just a pure little gem in this shitty world and I love it so much omg, I want to cry all over again. <br /><br />AND LET'S TALK ABOUT LABELS AND JUDGEMENT!!!! One of the greatest things about this book is the message about shitty labels people smack onto you. Our MC Declan Murphy is known for his bad reputation for drunk driving, getting into an accident and then being put in jail. Everyone shit talks about him going to prison. <br /><br /><b>But no one</b> cares to think about what he went through. Why he was in an accident and what <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[childhood abuse <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> caused that to happen. No one gives a fuck about what you go through, and are very quick to judge you. They don't care that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ your sister died and you could've prevented the death. They don't care about the guilt and pain you carry. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>So like, DON'T JUDGE A BOOK BY ITS COVER?????</b> Ever heard of that folks?<br /><br />There's so many twists and secrets revealed and it's just SO FUCKIGN CRAZY !!!<br /><br />Also CAN WE TALK ABOUT THAT ENDING BECAUSE WHAT THE FUCK I FEEL CHEATED ON. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AFTER EVERYTHING THEY GO THROUGH WE ONLY GET ONCE FUCKING KISS THAT ISN'T EVEN DETAILED AND SO SHORT AND AKDSKDALHF I'M FUCKING RIOTING. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, if you love me please read this, I'll pay you. <br /><br />----<br />YOU, *points at you* <i>STOP</i> WHATEVER THE FUCK YOU'RE DOING. AND PICK THIS BOOK UP. AND FUCKING READ IT.<br /><br />you're welcome.</span>

<div id="review_1949707615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1949707615" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1949707615?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1949707615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3825691726838796298">I WASN'T SUPPOSED TO READ THIS BOOK IN ONE SITTING BUT I DID BECAUSE I COULDN'T STOP READING AND AHHHHHHHHH I'M SO HAPPY AND I CAN'T STOP SMILING AND WANTING TO CRY AND HUG THIS BOOK TO MY CHEST ALL AT THE SAME TIME AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH *incoherent blubber*<br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/03/review-letters-to-lost-by-brigid.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Letters to the Lost by Brigid Kemmerer<br/>Publisher: Bloomsbury USA Childrens<br/>Publication Date: April 4, 2017<br/>Rating: 5 stars<br/>Source: eARC from N</span>
  <span id="freeText3825691726838796298" style="display:none">I WASN'T SUPPOSED TO READ THIS BOOK IN ONE SITTING BUT I DID BECAUSE I COULDN'T STOP READING AND AHHHHHHHHH I'M SO HAPPY AND I CAN'T STOP SMILING AND WANTING TO CRY AND HUG THIS BOOK TO MY CHEST ALL AT THE SAME TIME AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH *incoherent blubber*<br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/03/review-letters-to-lost-by-brigid.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Letters to the Lost by Brigid Kemmerer<br />Publisher: Bloomsbury USA Childrens<br />Publication Date: April 4, 2017<br />Rating: 5 stars<br />Source: eARC from NetGalley<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Juliet Young always writes letters to her mother, a world-traveling photojournalist. Even after her mother's death, she leaves letters at her grave. It's the only way Juliet can cope.<br /><br />Declan Murphy isn't the sort of guy you want to cross. In the midst of his court-ordered community service at the local cemetery, he's trying to escape the demons of his past.<br /><br />When Declan reads a haunting letter left beside a grave, he can't resist writing back. Soon, he's opening up to a perfect stranger, and their connection is immediate. But neither Declan nor Juliet knows that they're not actually strangers. When life at school interferes with their secret life of letters, sparks will fly as Juliet and Declan discover truths that might tear them apart.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />I've read all six of Kemmerer's previous novels (and some of the novellas too), and for the most part, I enjoyed all of what I read. Kemmerer has a way of writing broken teens who are trying to find their way. But I think Kemmerer is at her best, with this book. This, to me, is her best work. This book split me open and made my heart hurt - in the best of ways. I wouldn't say that I get emotional over books, but this one made me feel some feels. <br /><br />This is Juliet Young's and Declan Murphy's stories, which becomes one story. Juliet's mother died in a hit-and-run car crash, and she has been grieving ever since. Juliet used to write letters to her mom since her mother was often overseas, as a photographer in war zones and such. And so Juliet continues to write letters to her mom, but leaves them at the grave site. Declan Murphy has community service, which involves mowing and lawn of the cemetery. He finds one of the letters at a grave site, reads it, and writes back. An exchange of letters occurs, and then it becomes emails. Juliet and Declan have no idea that they are reaching out to each other and helping each other through their grief and pain. But in real life, Juliet misjudges Declan, and Declan misjudges Juliet. Both are not the other's biggest fans; but when one finds out that the other is the letter writer, will it matter?<br /><br />I sat down with this book with the intention of reading only half of the book, and saving the other half for the next day. I started reading really late into the night (after 9 PM) and had no intention of finishing. But hours went by, my family went to bed, and I didn't even notice. I was so engrossed in this book, and I couldn't stop reading, and the next thing I know, I've finished it. It was that wonderful, and heartbreaking, and thought-provoking. <br /><br />Usually when there is a YA book with dual, first-person POVs, I adore one of them, and feel so-so about the other (I don't have this problem with adult books, which is a relief). With this book, I liked both characters a lot. I think I liked Declan more, and I really connected him more (for some reason - it's not like I have a stepparent or a father in prison or a shred of the problems he has). <br /><br />Declan is so misjudged, and by everyone. Everyone labels him as a thug and a criminal, and when someone says something bad about him, no one comes to his defense. If he is anywhere near a bad situation, it gets blamed on him. He and his stepfather practically hate each other, and his mother is so passive and doesn't even talk to him. His sister is dead, his father is in jail, and he has to work off ninety hours of community service for one very bad decision. But... Declan isn't a bad guy. He has an attitude and he doesn't hide his anger, but he isn't a terrible person. He has a strong sense of morals and he is very intelligent, But again, misjudged. Even - and especially - by our heroine, Juliet.<br /><br />Juliet is overwhelmed with grief. Her mother's death is still fresh, and even the thought of getting rid of her mother's cameras makes Juliet break down in tears, or panic. Juliet hasn't had an easy year, but she isn't alone. She misjudges Declan badly, and slowly, she starts to realize that. Juliet is a good girl, though at first she is a little judgmental (towards Declan). In general she isn't... but to him, she was. She was to the point where she was afraid of him, which I thought was silly. <br /><br />To me, it's a testament to Kemmerer's talent as a writer, how she can characterize these two teens so well, and bring about those fears and angers and pain so well, such that the reader is incredibly aware of them. There wasn't a chapter that went by that I didn't distinctly feel Declan's fury and his hurt, or Juliet's panic and grief. Such good writing, in terms of the development of these two characters.<br /><br />The letter-writing aspect of the story was so wonderful. At first it was odd - Juliet was furious to find out that someone wrote on her private letter to her dead mother. But then the letter-writing turned into something more meaningful and necessary. Both characters had a lot of pain and hurt to work through, and the anonymous letter-writing really helped. Imagine being able to lay out your big problems, your little problems, your crappy day, to someone who knows exactly nothing about you. Someone who knows nothing, and yet everything. Letter-writing isn't new in YA (P.S. I Like You by Kasie West, Tell Me Three Things by Julie Buxbaum...), but it's a concept that I adore so much.<br /><br />This is YA contemporary with a lot of "tough issues" explored. Declan's relationship with his stepfather, with his mother, Juliet's relationship with her father, Declan's crime and his community service, his anger, Juliet's grief, Juliet's judgment of Declan... there is a lot to unload and handle, in this book. The most meaningful (or one of them) was Kemmerer's message about misjudging people - someone like Declan will get blamed and beat down because people already expect him to be a bad person, a thug and a criminal, but that isn't fair and it isn't right.<br /><br />There is romance and it's both there and it's not. Letter-writing Declan and letter-writing Juliet definitely fall for each other through letters - their connection is very powerful. In-person Declan and in-person Juliet have more of a slow-burn, hate-to-love romance. They bicker and fight nearly every time they see each other, and they constantly snipe at each other and misjudge each other. But their relationship changes a lot. There is a lot of chemistry between them, but it's often off the page. I liked the romance, despite the "physical" side of the romance not really being there.<br /><br />There were a lot of wonderful secondary characters in this book! Rev, Declan's best friend, who has a heartbreaking past but a positive outlook on life. He is an amazing friend and I loved their bromance. He's one of my favorites, and I can't wait to read his story next. Rowan, Juliet's best friend, who is so supportive and such a good best friend. Then there is "Melonhead" (his name is Frank), who is Declan's community service supervisor. He actually plays a huge and very positive role in Declan's life, and I'm glad he is in the story. Same with Rev's parents. Positive role models - not like Declan's mother and stepfather. Ugh, to both of them. <br /><br />The ending is perfect! Things work out well for Declan in many areas of his life. It's not like all of his problems are fixed overnight, but he takes a lot of baby steps in the right direction. Same with Juliet. And of course, same for the two of them, in terms of togetherness. Although, I have to say, we need an epilogue, or a loooooot of cameo appearances in Rev's book. There is a distinct lack of physical swoon that needs to be made up for, in Rev's book!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />The only thing I wanted more of was the thing I just mentioned - more physical swoon. I shared a snippet of this book on my latest Swoon Thursday post, and notice how it isn't a kissy swoon! Yeah, there could have been more kissy scenes. A lot more.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />YA contemporary fan or not (I'm not one), I recommend this book. It is such a meaningful and thought-provoking book. Also, I can't remember the last time I got that swept up in a story, to the point where I unintentionally finish it or stay up really late without being aware. (I stay up late reading books all the time but it's always intentional). There are a lot of tough topics explored in this book, but it's not overwhelmingly heavy. This is an excellent story that is powerful beyond it being a YA contemporary story about two teens who meet in more than one way.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded up to 5 stars (a rare 5 stars from me!). I am incredibly excited to read Rev's book next year! So far I'm seven for seven with Kemmerer's books and I have yet to be really disappointed. While I certainly do recommend her Elemental series, I recommend this book even more so! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3825691726838796298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12049759684220760434"><b>Vivid and heartbreaking</b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560527983ra/27668709.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>I feel like a bad friend, but I can't help it. I can't force what I'm feeling to fit between chapters two and six in some handbook dealing with the death of a loved one.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1580920531ra/28908920.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Letters to the Lost</i>, follows the lives of two teenagers in the wake of personal tragedies. <br/><br/>Through very odd circumstances they begin a correspondence, initially through handwritten letters left in a local cemetery, and eventually through dummy email accounts. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508942248ra/24268919.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Since neither one is aware of the identity of </span>
  <span id="freeText12049759684220760434" style="display:none"><b>Vivid and heartbreaking</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560527983ra/27668709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I feel like a bad friend, but I can't help it. I can't force what I'm feeling to fit between chapters two and six in some handbook dealing with the death of a loved one.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1580920531ra/28908920.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Letters to the Lost</i>, follows the lives of two teenagers in the wake of personal tragedies. <br><br>Through very odd circumstances they begin a correspondence, initially through handwritten letters left in a local cemetery, and eventually through dummy email accounts. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508942248ra/24268919.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Since neither one is aware of the identity of the other, they feel able to be completely open and honest about their feelings and experiences. <br><br>What transpires is an absolutely stunning portrayal of the <b>power of friendship</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545272228ra/26774389.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After the sudden, tragic loss of her mother, Juliet shuts herself off from the world. <br><br>She is struggling with an overwhelming sense of grief, combined with guilt and fear of never being able to live up to her mother's legacy. <br><br>Every day she goes to the cemetery and visits her mother's gravesite, leaving letters for her that she believes will never be read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517595246ra/24990833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Declan is a quintessential 'bad boy' or so he would have you believe. He is dealing with his own tragedy, the loss of his sister and the subsequent imprisonment of his father. <br><br>Feeling abandoned by his mother, who has since gone on to remarry a complete jerk, he struggles with his own feelings of guilt, isolation and anger. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469768789ra/19855171.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Forced to do community service work after his own drunk driving incident, Declan ends up working on the maintenance crew at the local cemetery where he stumbles upon Juliet's letters.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1548367192ra/26966448.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Watching the relationship between these two develop is absolutely beautiful. I cannot express it any better than that. <br><br>I was completely blown away by Brigid Kemmerer's writing. She is so talented and I have already purchased the companion novel to this one, <i>More Than We Can Tell</i>, which follows one of my favorite characters from this book, Declan's misunderstood best friend, Rev.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446930728ra/16928560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you have been on the fence about picking this one up, please do. It is really just so stunning.<br><br>For anyone who has lost anyone under tragic circumstances, I think a lot of the text surrounding those feelings of grief and guilt are just so relatable and really, cathartic.<br><br>That's the way it felt for me anyway. This is definitely a book I would recommend to anyone and will probably end up reading again someday.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538394604ra/26382449.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2305766274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305766274" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305766274?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408883525" href="/book/show/33857632-letters-to-the-lost">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=alcoholism-drugs">alcoholism-drugs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305766274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9320274089848874008"><i> “One day isn’t your life…a day is just a day.” </i><br/><br/>Boy am I surprised with my rating!<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081453721?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sana's review</a> sums it up pretty well – I was expecting cheese, pointless teenage drama, a lot of sickening “I can’t live without you” melodrama, and not a whole lot else.<br/><br/>But I was WRONG guys. So wrong. This was full of pain and trauma, hope and love, desperation and fear, honesty and friendship. I cried. Real tears. Actual eye leakage. I can’t believe it.<br/><br/>So Juliet writes letters to her mother who died in a freak ca</span>
  <span id="freeText9320274089848874008" style="display:none"><i> “One day isn’t your life…a day is just a day.” </i><br /><br />Boy am I surprised with my rating!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081453721?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sana's review</a> sums it up pretty well – I was expecting cheese, pointless teenage drama, a lot of sickening “I can’t live without you” melodrama, and not a whole lot else.<br /><br />But I was WRONG guys. So wrong. This was full of pain and trauma, hope and love, desperation and fear, honesty and friendship. I cried. Real tears. Actual eye leakage. I can’t believe it.<br /><br />So Juliet writes letters to her mother who died in a freak car accident, she leaves them on her grave and that is that. Until one day she receives a reply. At first she is pissed off. Who does this person think they are? Reading her private letters and having the nerve to respond? But eventually they start a pen pal relationship and soon both are spilling their darkest secrets.<br /><br />Declan Murphy is a loser with a record. At least that is all anyone sees when they look at him. He got drunk and wrecked his dad’s truck. No one cares why he did this, or what could have been going through his mind – he is just written off, by everyone except his best friend Rev. When he reads a letter left at one of the graves during his Community Service he connects with the writing and understands the pain within it, he can’t help but respond.<br /><br />As Juliet (Cemetary Girl) and Declan (The Dark) move their letters to the electronic world of email (I got serious A Cinderella Story vibes – love that film!) Juliet and Declan actually do meet in real life, not that they know who the other person really is to them. And they can’t stand one another!<br /><br />Usually I don’t get the whole enemies to lovers thing, if you don’t like someone to begin with – I think there’s probably a reason for it. HOWEVER, in this instance they really don’t know one another (apart from secretly, which neither of them has worked out haha) they only know OF one another, and the parts of themselves they choose to show the world which isn’t NEARLY enough to get even a snapshot of their real lives and emotions.<br /><br />I also loved that the romance took a back seat. This wasn’t a “romance fixes everything” story. This was two people, struggling with some really dark stuff – finding solace in writing down their thoughts and feelings to someone else. There were plenty of shocks and twists along the way (which I honestly didn’t expect at all), truly great friendships and at its heart, a feeling that we are never alone.<br /><br />I loved it, and my eyes were misty. Also shout out to Warda whose shining review convinced me to pick this up in the first place :) &lt;3 <br /><br /><i> “I thank whatever gods may be for my unconquerable soul.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9320274089848874008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2255176802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2255176802" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255176802?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255176802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15147411286432977283">I’m beginning to think I have a different idea of what’s emotional because I am yet again baffled by the lack of intense emotions I was supposed to have felt reading this. According to the reviews, I should be heartbroken right now. Destroyed. Spent. Instead, I was BORED. I’m sorry but I. Was. Bored. Out of my mind. <br/><br/>I appreciate the premise of the book, it deals with grief, anger, guilt, as well as healing and acceptance. To be able to move on and begin anew. All of which sounded so enticing yet</span>
  <span id="freeText15147411286432977283" style="display:none">I’m beginning to think I have a different idea of what’s emotional because I am yet again baffled by the lack of intense emotions I was supposed to have felt reading this. According to the reviews, I should be heartbroken right now. Destroyed. Spent. Instead, I was BORED. I’m sorry but I. Was. Bored. Out of my mind. <br /><br />I appreciate the premise of the book, it deals with grief, anger, guilt, as well as healing and acceptance. To be able to move on and begin anew. All of which sounded so enticing yet something was amiss. It didn’t tug at my heart strings as I’d hoped. I also hated the execution and one of the main leads. <br /><br />First off, <b>NOTHING HAPPENED in this book. NOTHING.</b> The two MCs wrote letters back and forth to each other, talked about their grief (which I can certainly appreciate) but... that was about it. Not much else aside from this happened. <br /><br />Second, I loved and felt for Declan so much but it took about the first 30 pages for Juliet and myself to get on the wrong side of each other. It was never the same after that. <br />Her hostile and petty attitude deterred me from fully enjoying the novel and forming any kind of emotional connection with her. To say I hated her would be a gross understatement. So much so that I wanted to skip all her POVs and only read Declan’s but I get stressed out about skipping parts in books so I pushed through it by the skin of my teeth. <br /><br />She makes so many horrible assumptions about people she knows nothing about and says things that simply make you cringe and want to scream - just STFU! All it takes her is a single second to form a despicable opinion by which point she precedes to judge them based off of second hand rumours, their look, attire choices, etc... <br /><br /><b>I loath judgmental characters. If there’s one sure way to guarantee my instant loss of interest, it’s presenting me with presumptuous, judgmental characters.</b> Juliet was the worst kind of judgmental. She’d throw these petty and hateful remarks at people then blames everyone and gets angry about it when her hostile, antagonistic remarks are not received with grace.<br />She was aggravating and despicable to the max and I loathed her with a passion. I could not stand her. <br />She got better in the second half but by then the damage had already been done. <br /><br />Declan, the second perspective, who was also tormented with grief &amp; guilt, and his kind, gentle and supportive best friend Rev were the only redeeming qualities of this book. <br /><br />All in all, it was alright. By no means groundbreaking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15147411286432977283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8794780890911545960">You know when you <b>need</b> a book but you’re not even sure <b>what</b> you exactly need and then you win some theoretical lottery bc YOU PICKED THE RIGHT DAMN BOOK<br/><br/>That’s me right now.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499826898i/23272081._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a href='http://phantomrin.tumblr.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>(s)</a> <br/><br/>I’m LEGIT a sucker for anything resembling <i>You’ve Got Mail</i> (you can blame <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Peppa Pig</a> for that). This is like my 5th <s>retelling</s> book with a similar plot and gosh damn give me more.<br/>	<br/>But honestly this book was so much more than just passing cute notes back and forth, it was about sorrow and grief and friendship and family and g</span>
  <span id="freeText8794780890911545960" style="display:none">You know when you <b>need</b> a book but you’re not even sure <b>what</b> you exactly need and then you win some theoretical lottery bc YOU PICKED THE RIGHT DAMN BOOK<br><br>That’s me right now.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499826898i/23272081._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://phantomrin.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">(s)</a> <br><br>I’m LEGIT a sucker for anything resembling <i>You’ve Got Mail</i> (you can blame <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Peppa Pig</a> for that). This is like my 5th <s>retelling</s> book with a similar plot and gosh damn give me more.<br>	<br>But honestly this book was so much more than just passing cute notes back and forth, it was about sorrow and grief and friendship and family and giving yourself a second chance. Oh my Lord, there were so many touching and inspirational moments. THESE KIDS KILL ME.<br><br><i> I shrug and try not to make this seem like a big deal. “There’s always tomorrow.”<br>“Yeah,” he agrees. “There’s always tomorrow.”</i><br><br>The writing was SO easy to read, it was engaging, entertaining, captivating and beyond all, EVERYTHING I FRICKEN NEEDED RIGHT NOW. <br><br>And you know how when you have these kind of stories you always assume the boy will come and save the girl. Like bam they meet, kiss kiss, and all the sadness goes away, <b>but it wasn’t like that</b> <br><br>They didn’t instantly solve each other’s problems in a single hallway glance it was like they encouraged and supported each other from behind anonymous usernames but they still had to work it out on their own and reach their own closure <br><br>But it’s not <b>all</b> grief. Letters to the Lost was also funny and cute, I mean <b>really</b> cute like I was clutching my heart and squealing like a literal 6 year old and im not even ashamed about it<br><br>The characters are so utterly fricken flawed and it’s absolutely refreshing and so brilliant. Also, Rev is my son and I need to see more of his adorable face plz. <br><br>Also for a contemporary, this sure does have a lot of twists and turns and they’re so unexpected that when it hits you, you’re like W H O A ! ! *screams into the void for 13 hours*<br><br>Basically, I just want everyone in the world to read this book bc it made me so fricken happy <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499826898i/23272082._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://phantomrin.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">(s)</a> <br><br>Gahhhh, I’m going to go participate in some existentialist stuff bc I can’t handle that I finished the book so quickly. Need more ;-;<br><br><i> “We're all united by grief, and somehow divided by the same thing.”</i><br><br>5 stars!!</span>

<div id="review_2643404674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2643404674" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2643404674?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-audio">2018-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2018-ya-challenge">2018-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2643404674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5373197174717243678"><b>5 stars</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_2849_zpsqwjw78up.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1546793228i/26870834._SY540_.png' alt=' photo IMG_2849_zpsqwjw78up.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“One day isn't your whole life. A day is just a day.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><i>Letters to the Lost</i> is a stunning story about grief, moving on, and seeing past the ordinary. It’s a beautiful coming of age story that gave me so many feels. I adored it. <br/><br/>Juliet and Declan couldn’t seem more different if they tried. They go to the same high school, but they don’t run in the same crowds. Declan is a bad boy, and Juliet is a good student, into photography, and outgoing. Or she used to be, until she lost </span>
  <span id="freeText5373197174717243678" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b> <br><br><a href="https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/IMG_2849_zpsqwjw78up.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1546793228i/26870834._SY540_.png" alt=" photo IMG_2849_zpsqwjw78up.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“One day isn't your whole life. A day is just a day.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><i>Letters to the Lost</i> is a stunning story about grief, moving on, and seeing past the ordinary. It’s a beautiful coming of age story that gave me so many feels. I adored it. <br><br>Juliet and Declan couldn’t seem more different if they tried. They go to the same high school, but they don’t run in the same crowds. Declan is a bad boy, and Juliet is a good student, into photography, and outgoing. Or she used to be, until she lost her mom. Declan and Juliet first ‘meet’ when Declan is doing his community service and finds a letter at a grave. He can relate, so he writes back. This turns into a pen-pal relationship of sorts. <br><br><br>The letters. The emails. The communication between Declan and Juliet. That was my favorite part of the story. I loved watching them connect, trust one another, relate to one another, and start to fall for one another, without having any idea who each one is. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“Do you believe in fate? Sometimes I want to. I want to believe that we all walk some path toward… something, and our paths intertwine for a reason. Like this, the way we’ve found each other. The way you told me the right story when I so desperately needed to hear it.”</blockquote>
</i>  The connection that these two characters had was something. It just shows you that opposites truly do attract sometimes, and people are so much more than what they seem. I read Rev’s book before this one, so I already kind of knew Declan, but I loved seeing more of his story. His past broke my heart. The pain, grief, and responsibility he felt was crushing. And Juliet is also drowning in grief. These two needed each other more than they ever could have known. <br><br> I just have to make a note that I listened to the audio book of this, and Kirby Heybourne voiced Declan. Kirby also voices Josh in TSOT and let me tell you, his voice is magical. He doesn’t just narrate, you feel the characters through him. I can’t even explain it, he does an amazing job voice acting and I can’t recommend listening to this one enough. Brittany Pressely also does a good job voicing Juliet. <br><br>Brigid Kemmerer, if you haven’t read her, you need to. She has a new fan in me. I’ve loved both of the books I’ve read by this author, but this, by far, is my favorite. Moving, heart-wrenching, and gave me all the feels. Truly, my best YA book of 2018 and a must read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5373197174717243678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1857996631" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1857996631" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1857996631?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857996631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6891647103634457514">Had they not lost someone important in their lives, Declan and Juliet never would have connected.<br/><br/>But they have, and now they need each other’s support.<br/><br/>LETTERS TO THE LOST held my attention considerably well. Honestly, I thought I was in somewhat of a book slump, before I picked this book up, because I couldn’t bring myself to finish the other books I had started.<br/><br/>But maybe it wasn’t me. Maybe those books in question were the problem. Or maybe Brigid Kemmerer’s new novel saved me. For that, I am e</span>
  <span id="freeText6891647103634457514" style="display:none">Had they not lost someone important in their lives, Declan and Juliet never would have connected.<br /><br />But they have, and now they need each other’s support.<br /><br />LETTERS TO THE LOST held my attention considerably well. Honestly, I thought I was in somewhat of a book slump, before I picked this book up, because I couldn’t bring myself to finish the other books I had started.<br /><br />But maybe it wasn’t me. Maybe those books in question were the problem. Or maybe Brigid Kemmerer’s new novel saved me. For that, I am extremely grateful.<br /><br />It’s a dramatic story. Do not pick this up if you want to smile, laugh or swoon. There’s drama throughout the story. It even gets melodramatic in the end, which is something that made me cringe a little. <br /><br />It’s emotional all the way. A little clichéd here and there, what with Declan’s stepfather being a douche and for the two main characters to interact actively online, while offline they’re avoiding each other.<br /><br />I believed it. It’s a convincing enough story. It does come off as far-fetched in the beginning, with the exchange of letters, making the hero and heroine think that they are meant to find one another, but as the story progresses, the *situation* becomes less coincidental and more relevant to the plot.<br /><br />Declan is not someone to whom I really warmed up. He’s fine. He’s a teenager who feels uncomfortable in his own house. Of course he’s going to be defensive and angry, and overall, pretty unpleasant. I understand. But that doesn’t mean I’m going to like the guy. I prefer my heroes less aggressive, verbally as much as physically.<br /><br />Juliet is a very realistic teenage girl. All the characters are, by the way. It’s not because I didn’t love them that they were bad. I connected with Juliet the most because her grief felt real to me. Part of me felt sorry for her loss, but another part of me admired her strength and willingness to move on, although it proved to be extremely difficult for her. Baby steps. <br /><br />LETTERS TO THE LOST is a good story, but not the most original one there is.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6891647103634457514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1875762798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875762798" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875762798?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875762798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6981817539333241379">3.5 stars rounded up to a 4<br/><br/>"Me Too" are words we are currently hearing a lot in the media, and these two words also pack a powerful punch in this book.<br/><br/>Juliet Young has always written letters to her mother who traveled the world as a photojournalist. When her Mother dies, Juliet continues writing her letters without thinking the letters will ever be answered. Then one day a letter was answered with two words "Me Too"<br/><br/>Two simple words that have a lot of meaning. Just who has answered back and why?<br/><br/>D</span>
  <span id="freeText6981817539333241379" style="display:none">3.5 stars rounded up to a 4<br /><br />"Me Too" are words we are currently hearing a lot in the media, and these two words also pack a powerful punch in this book.<br /><br />Juliet Young has always written letters to her mother who traveled the world as a photojournalist. When her Mother dies, Juliet continues writing her letters without thinking the letters will ever be answered. Then one day a letter was answered with two words "Me Too"<br /><br />Two simple words that have a lot of meaning. Just who has answered back and why?<br /><br />Declan Murphy finds a letter left on a grave, curious he reads it and decides to answer back. Because he can relate to what is written. He is surprised when he gets an answer back.<br /><br />Neither Juliet nor Declan know who the other is, they never write their names on their letters. Not knowing who the other person they are writing to makes it easier for both open up and share their thoughts and feelings but what they don't know is that they have met. <br /><br />This book is YA but is easily enjoyed by all. Juliet is the good girl and Declan is the "bad boy". But is this your typical good girl-bad boy book? I liked how the Author shows how our perceptions of others can get in the way of our interactions with them. just because someone does something wrong, does that make them bad for life or just someone who made a mistake? If someone is quiet and sullen is it because they are cold and indifferent, or could it be because they are in pain or suffering? What happens when you build an invisible wall around yourself and begin to let someone inside your barriers, when you let someone see your true self?<br /><br />This book is also not your typical YA romance because both characters are dealing with grief. They both have sadness and loss in their lives. Both are trying to cope in their own way while silently reaching out to the other through their letters.<br /><br />Some of the book is a little cliché - troubled bad boy with evil step-parent but that is easily overlooked in lieu of plot. I liked how this book dealt with grief, family issues, setting aside your boundaries, showing who you really are, being vulnerable, acceptance, trust, second chances, friendship, and young love.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6981817539333241379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1954599513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954599513" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1954599513?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954599513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16140620467440755290"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954599513' rel='nofollow noopener'>Letters to the Lost</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2225814693' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than We Can Tell</a> ★★★☆☆</blockquote><br/>I’d heard somewhat mixed reviews from my friends on this book, but after learning that the ARC of Brigid’s I’d been approved for, <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2225814693' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Than We Can Tell</a>,</i> is meant to be read after this one, I decided to go ahead and read it – and I couldn’t put it down. Don’t get me wrong, <i>Letters</i> is an incredibly sad story filled with grief, pain, and regret, but there’s also something tremendously heart-warming and comforting in Brigid’s writing.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“What</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText16140620467440755290" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954599513" rel="nofollow noopener">Letters to the Lost</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2225814693" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than We Can Tell</a> ★★★☆☆</blockquote><br />I’d heard somewhat mixed reviews from my friends on this book, but after learning that the ARC of Brigid’s I’d been approved for, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2225814693" rel="nofollow noopener">More Than We Can Tell</a>,</i> is meant to be read after this one, I decided to go ahead and read it – and I couldn’t put it down. Don’t get me wrong, <i>Letters</i> is an incredibly sad story filled with grief, pain, and regret, but there’s also something tremendously heart-warming and comforting in Brigid’s writing.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“What you wrote implies that you understand agony. I don’t think you do. If you did, you wouldn’t have interfered with mine.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I’m such a sucker for romances and friendships that form through written correspondence, but I don’t think I’ve ever seen it done while being intermingled with an enemies-to-lovers trope, and this book executes it in such a fun, captivating way. From the start, Juliet and Declan can hardly stand each other – Juliet is self-absorbed and terrified of his large stature and stoic, harsh mannerisms, while Declan has written her off as just another pretty girl who thinks she’s out of his league.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“When everything goes to hell around you, the only way to go is forward.”</i>
</blockquote><br />While I honestly loved Declan from the beginning – I have such a soft spot for angsty, hurting “bad boys” – Juliet was fairly unlikable at the start, mostly due to the way she treats the people around her. She’s hurting, and her mother’s passing is recent, so she lashes out constantly, whether it’s at Declan, her father, or her friends. The thing about her behavior, though, is you can’t help but empathize for her even when she’s at her worst.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“One day isn't your whole life. A day is just a day.”</i>
</blockquote><br />It takes some time for Juliet to come around, but Declan is the shining star of character development in this story, if you ask me. In the beginning, he’s at the edge of a cliff, and it’s taking everything in him to make it through one day at a time. He’s living with guilt that nobody should bear, being harassed by his step-father and forgotten by his mother in the wake of his younger sister’s passing. There were moments in his narrative where I was so worried about what would happen to him, but he becomes so strong, and under all the pain and rage is this mushy little teddy bear that just wants to protect the people he loves.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Sometimes I think fate conspires against us. Or maybe fate conspires with us.</i>
</blockquote> <br />Of course, I can’t review this book without talking about Declan’s best friend, Rev, who is hilarious, awkward, precious, and a delightful addition to every scene he’s in. I loved his character so much, and I didn’t realize until after finishing this book that he’s the star of the follow-up story, so now I’m twice as excited for that one as I already was. I can’t wait to see where life takes him next, and to get to know him and his sordid past a little bit better.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “You’re okay,” he says again. I like that, how he’s so sure. Not, “Are you okay?” No question about it. You’re okay.</i>
</blockquote><br />If you enjoy YA contemporaries about grief and healing, or if you’re just like me and you can’t resist a good falling-in-love-through-emails trope, pick this one up right away – you won’t regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16140620467440755290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
