    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2089468060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2089468060" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2089468060?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to elena by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2089468060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6748656313634376867"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>We're all united by grief, and somehow divided by the same thing.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Don't you just love being so excited to start reading again after a reading slump of like, 3 months or so, and then ending up not enjoying the book at all? <b>Because I sure do not.</b> When I picked up Letters to the Lost, I didn't expect anything from it. My friend Sana recommended it to me after she read some cute contemporaries recommended by her friend. When I first read the synopsis of it, I did get intrigued because it </span>
  <span id="freeText6748656313634376867" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>We're all united by grief, and somehow divided by the same thing.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Don't you just love being so excited to start reading again after a reading slump of like, 3 months or so, and then ending up not enjoying the book at all? <b>Because I sure do not.</b> When I picked up Letters to the Lost, I didn't expect anything from it. My friend Sana recommended it to me after she read some cute contemporaries recommended by her friend. When I first read the synopsis of it, I did get intrigued because it was short and simple but it as surely captivating in a way. The whole <i>Juliet forgetting about her mother's loss and Declan moving past his haunting demons</i> grabbed by attention, but it sure did not remain. In fact, it was lost in the first 10 pages.<br /><br />Letters to the Lost is about two characters who are struggling with grief and loss and torture to themselves. <b>Juliet Young</b> is trying to move on from her mother's loss even though she feels like she's drowning in the grief. She wants to know what happened and why. She used to do this thing with her mother, who was a photographer and would travel, where she would send letters to her mother and her mother would send them back. In one of the days her mother was gone, Juliet found out her mother would not return, and she decided to not send the letter to her mother. Instead, she left it in her mother's cemetery. She no longer sent letters. She no longer touched cameras. She no longer took a picture. She didn't do anything that would bring her back memories of her mother. Then we have <b>Declan Murphy</b> who is completely judged and labeled for something he did. After Declan crashed his father's pick up truck into a building, he's been judged in negative ways by his peers, his teachers, and even his family members. He has one friend who is like a brother to him who also has his own haunting past called Rev and is the one person Declan trusts the most. Declan wanted people (and himself) to forget about what happened. There's a story behind it all, but some people just seem to not care and move on and believe what they hear.<br /><br />One day, Juliet leaves her last letter in her mother's cemetery and, not expecting anyone to see and pick it up, Declan comes and read the later and decides to write her back. This angers Juliet and gets her anrgy at how someone could invade her privacy and just write back to her without knowing who she was and now knowing her story. But, Juliet and Declan keep talking to each other, although they don't know. They know each other in real life but they actually hate each other. In the letters, the begin to email each other as <b>Cemetery Girl and The Dark</b> with no one knowing who is who. As time passes, they begin to write to each other and are open to each other as never before. The begin to understand each other's paths and feel some sort of connection between strangers. This fate may lead to secrets being untold, but that just might lead to lies being as threats. <br /><br />I expected <i>Letters to the Lost</i> to feel real for me. I expected to feel sympathy for the characters in a way--to feel bad for them. <b>I didn't feel anything though.</b> I didn't cry. I didn't laugh. I didn't smile. I had my resting bitch face the whole time reading this, and I hated it. I predicted things since the beginning, and sure I was wrong in most, but I still hated how they connected in ways. I didn't hate any character, but I also was not able to relate to any character in any way and I was not able to sympathize in them. Most of the time, I can understand what the main character is going through or what it feels like to go through what they are going through, but not in this one. The book is supposed to make you cry and make you feel sorry to the characters. It's supposed to show you what it feels like <b>to be judged and labeled when no one even knows you and your story</b>. I didn't feel bad for the characters in the beginning or the end, especially in the end with what happened, and I don't regret it. I know it's sad for someone to lose a mother and I know it's sad to be seen as someone you are not, but in the end, none of it was true.<br /><br />I admittedly didn't feel bad for any character. I actually felt pity for Declan's attitude and personality and Juliet's judgemental phase. They both were two different characters, and they both had their negative features. Declan was an asshole to Juliet even when she tried to be nice. I always wondered why, but it might've been because she was judgemental of him. Even when she and every other classmate didn't know Declan's full story, they would judge and criticize him for what they heard. They would make fun of him and his father who is in jail. They would make fun of Declan because he was put in jail as well even when they don't know what happened. I guess you could say there was a good enough reason for Declan to be an asshole to everyone because of his label, <b>but I still wish he could've like stood up to something about it to bring it down.</b> Instead, he'd just walk away and not bother to care about anyone or anything. Juliet was a normal teenager grl who would judge someone based on its cover. She didn't know Declan at all and would also go along with what she heard. But then, I didn't feel a lot of pity for her as much. She lost her mother and didn't know why and she was the normal teenage girl who acted the same and would try to start her path over.<br /><br />This is supposed to be a <b>contemporary romance</b>, but the romance is <b>not there at all!</b> There are the last few pages, but they don't even count. There was nothing. If you know me, you know I'm a loser for cute contemporaries because I like crying about the cute relationship that I will never be able to have, and you'd expect me to read this book because of the romance. And yeah, that's right, but it wasn't there, and that was a problem. The romance isn't the main focus, but it wasn't a focus at all! Declan and Juliet's friendship developed and improved in a way that was confusing and not understandable. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Declan found out Cemetery Girl was Juliet first but didn't tell her and kept pretending to be someone else <i>as</i> The Dark, but then he slowly started falling in love with her. He was still an asshole at times even when he knew, and other times he was this sweet and caring boy. It didn't make sense to me! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Yes, there is character development which is why I'm giving this 2 stars and not 1. Declan improved more than Juliet and I loved that about him. He started building up his path and starting acting differently. He managed to listen to Juliet about his mother and stepfather and somehow confronted his own self. He was seen as cold and angry in the outside, but inside, <b>Declan was always caring, sweet, and funny.</b> Juliet had her improvement as well but decided to get back to taking pictures and even touching her mother's camera. She and her father actually managed to have a stable and healthy relationship even when she got mad at him. He wasn't the kind of father that would treat her differently and rudely because the mom was no longer there but instead, he'd try to treat her better. Her dad was caring as well and I'm glad both characters had healthy relationships with at least one parent.<br /><br />In my opinion, the best character in this story was Declan's best friend, <b>Rev.</b> Rev was outgoing and chill about everything. He didn't approach anyone with an angry attitude and showed his good side before others could show their own side. He was understanding for and to Declan and their relationship as friends were so cute. He wasn't angry and although he also has his own haunting and dark past, he can get past his emo looking phase and actually be seen as someone who has already managed to create their own path and continue to. <b>I did hear that this author is gonna publish a book about Rev, and yes, you bet I will read that!</b><br /><br />I actually own this author's other book, <i>Thicker than Water</i> and I kind of am interested in reading it but at the same time, I'm not sure. The writing in this was very easy to follow that I ended up reading as much as I could manage without realizing it. I haven't had time to read lately which was why I was surprised I managed to read at least 100 pages thanks to that 45 minute trip to another city. Maybe I'll read this author's other novels to see how different (or similar) it is. <i>Letters to the Lost</i> was not my cup of tea. Characters felt too bland and the whole plot was boring. In the end, everything is put together and makes sense but it's also everywhere that you might have to go back to the beginning to understand. In the end, you might even have to go back to the middle to understand it as well. The ending was just awful and I wish there was more to it, but overall, <i>Letters to the Lost</i> was <b>dull and not something I would read again.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6748656313634376867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1967136219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1967136219" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1967136219?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1967136219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2643931392373563710"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491794290i/22447428.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>Juliet Young writes letters to her mother... and leaves them at her grave. <br/>She never imagined someone would write back...</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br/><br/>***DEEP BREATH*** This book intrigued me from the moment I read the blurb. I like to find balance among all the books I read and since recently I've read many lighter, sexier romances, I was craving something a little more heavy and serious. This book immediately came to mind because the blurb really stuck with me -- the idea of char</span>
  <span id="freeText2643931392373563710" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491794290i/22447428.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>Juliet Young writes letters to her mother... and leaves them at her grave. <br>She never imagined someone would write back...</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br><br>***DEEP BREATH*** This book intrigued me from the moment I read the blurb. I like to find balance among all the books I read and since recently I've read many lighter, sexier romances, I was craving something a little more heavy and serious. This book immediately came to mind because the blurb really stuck with me -- the idea of characters becoming close without ever having met or knowing each other's identities were fascinated me. When I opened it, I was captivated by the story in the first two pages and literally read it straight through to the end without stopping. <br><br>In tone and feeling, this <em>is</em> a very serious book. Deep. Thoughtful. Painful. Hopeful. And incredibly well written!! It’s a quiet but powerful story. It’s not a Romance but there is a love story. It’s more about PEOPLE. Friendship. Family. Love. Loss. More like mature YA fiction in terms of genre (the hero and heroine are both seventeen and in their last year of high school but have each survived experiences that made them sometimes seem older than their years) but I do want to reassure you that there is a happy ending. The writing was beautiful. It flowed so smoothly and I definitely know I'd want to read another book by this author just because she wrote it. I loved the vivid imagery and the way she conveyed emotion. I highlighted so many passages. The characters were complex and compelling. The story was intriguing, surprising, and ultimately deeply satisfying. In every way, this book was the perfect “change of pace” I'd been searching for and while it was very DIFFERENT than what I'd normally read/review, I loved it!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>Juliet Young always writes letters to her mother, a world-traveling photojournalist. Even after her mother's death, she leaves letters at her grave. It's the only way Juliet can cope. </strong>
  </em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>
    <strong>Declan Murphy isn't the sort of guy you want to cross. In the midst of his court-ordered community service at the local cemetery, he's trying to escape the demons of his past.</strong>
  </em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>
    <strong>When Declan reads a haunting letter left beside a grave, he can't resist writing back. Soon, he's opening up to a perfect stranger, and their connection is immediate. But neither Declan nor Juliet knows that they're not actually strangers...</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br><br>The letters they wrote to each other were so thought provoking. Many of them gave me chills and shivers. There's a raw honesty to opening up to someone who doesn't know you but that you feel you can trust. It's like you bare your soul without fear of judgement. Each letter had weight, if that makes sense. They just conveyed so much.<br><br>It's worth mentioning again how much I loved the writing. Not only was it beautiful, but the pacing of the story was on point -- always moving forward, no 'extra' scenes, no parts of the book that I wanted to skim. I felt very connected to this story the whole way through.<br><br>This story addresses a lot of important themes of friendship, loyalty, betrayal, family life, loss, healing, bullying, judgment, unfairness of societal standards, and struggling to find a place to belong and make amends. The heroine is struggling in a world without her mother -- a parent she'd lost to a dangerous job she kept choosing to return to even at the risk that one day it might leave her daughter without a mother. And the hero is struggling with loss as well, and judgement from everyone around him. He's automatically labeled as a screw up and lives life having to prove himself every step of the way and it's exhausting and demoralizing. But in the midst of their pain comes these moment of hope that give them reason to think that maybe they can help each other come through to the other side.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>Do you believe in fate? Sometimes I want to. I want to believe that we all walk some path toward… something, and our paths intertwine for a reason. Like this, the way we’ve found each other. The way you told me the right story when I so desperately needed to hear ti.</em>
</blockquote><br><br>Their anonymity allows them to open up to each other in ways they'd never have been able to face to face. It gives them a safe zone without judgement, labels, or bias. Just one person spilling their heart to another -- connecting, sharing, trying to rationalize, understand, come to terms with the things that have happened to them and the people they loved. All their letters had a profound impact on my but the revelations towards the end had my heart racing and I read as fast as I could. I really loved the way the ending came together.<br><br>I'd consider this to have been a really fantastic reading experience. It was a very well written with well developed characters. I rarely read this genre, but the way Juliet and Declan subtly fell in love with each other through their letters gave my romantic heart just enough to keep me happy. Ultimately, this was a complete change of pace from what I usually read but I loved it and would recommend it to anyone looking for something a little different!<br><br><strong>Rating: 4.5 stars! Standalone Mature YA Fiction.</strong><br><br> <br>	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/2p5OLXE" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buy LETTERS TO THE LOST (Kindle)</a></strong> <br>	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/2oFiNpd" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buy LETTERS TO THE LOST (Hardcover)</a></strong> <br> <br><br>__________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>

    <a title="Zain Otoom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom"><img alt="Zain Otoom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598878687p2/45136398.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146179540?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zain Otoom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zain Otoom" href="/user/show/45136398-zain-otoom">Zain Otoom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45136398-zain-otoom?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4116859972140713559"><b>Okay full five starts and added to favourites because I can’t stop thinking about this novel and how much I love it.</b><br/>***<br/><b>Rounding it up to five stars because I think it deserves it.</b> <br/>*takes deep breaths* <br/>I’m crying. This was so beautiful I can’t even, bro. My heart got broken, mended and melted multiple times. What I loved most was—also is the same thing that broke my heart—Declan’s struggle with the labels and how people kept judging him without really knowing much about him at all. And while he h</span>
  <span id="freeText4116859972140713559" style="display:none"><b>Okay full five starts and added to favourites because I can’t stop thinking about this novel and how much I love it.</b><br />***<br /><b>Rounding it up to five stars because I think it deserves it.</b> <br />*takes deep breaths* <br />I’m crying. This was so beautiful I can’t even, bro. My heart got broken, mended and melted multiple times. What I loved most was—also is the same thing that broke my heart—Declan’s struggle with the labels and how people kept judging him without really knowing much about him at all. And while he had his best friend with him, without parental support when they actually do exist, how lonely and sad is that? But it was dealt with so beautifully and realistically, and oh I loved it so much. I loved this book so much. <br />Not only that, while the characters were flawed, their development is on point. Not to mention, it’s also super cute and had a bunch of moments where I was squealing and giggling. <br />There’s so much to this book that I feel like no matter what I write I won’t do it justice. Just go read. I swear it’s worth it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3125616540581226005">5 stars! <br/><br/>I feel so lucky that so far all the YA books that I've read have been winners for me! I have to admit I haven't been reading too many of them lately since it's getting harder and harder to find good ones. But I want to say "this one, this one right here" is the reason I'll always read YA! "Letters To The Lost" was so much more than the blurb so so much more.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499589900ra/23247137.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So here it goes Juliette, has recently lost her mom she feels lost without her, and so she starts writing her letters and leaving t</span>
  <span id="freeText3125616540581226005" style="display:none">5 stars! <br><br>I feel so lucky that so far all the YA books that I've read have been winners for me! I have to admit I haven't been reading too many of them lately since it's getting harder and harder to find good ones. But I want to say "this one, this one right here" is the reason I'll always read YA! "Letters To The Lost" was so much more than the blurb so so much more.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499589900ra/23247137.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So here it goes Juliette, has recently lost her mom she feels lost without her, and so she starts writing her letters and leaving them at her grave. Declan, works at the cemetery and sees one of the letters and reads it he feels such a pull from Juliette's word that he writes back two words "me too" those words change everything. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499589900ra/23247138.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What starts as angry letters become a connection of two people that share painful loses. I want to say that this book's main focus is not romance per se but a bound between Juliette and Declan. It was heart breaking to see them both in despair trying to find a life line in moments when they were so lost. But through those letters they find each other. The courage and voice they had lost.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499590225ra/23247163.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I went trough so many emotions with this book and even cried tears of frustration I think it was a first for me. Both Juliette and Declan changed so much by the end. They both realized how they had misconceptions of not just each other but their parents. But also had a new appreciation of the ones they thought didn't deserve it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499590225ra/23247164.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Loved this book, well written, well paced with a wonderful message of how in our darkest moments just one person reaching out to you can make such a positive difference. Not of battling our fights but giving us the strength to do it ourselves. This book is definitely one of my favorites of 2017!❤️<br><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151303275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6155557199391291440"><u>Second Read</u> <br/><br/>It was good the first time, it was brilliant the second time. <br/><br/>Brigid Kemmerer amazes me everytime. I forgot how addictive her writing is and how lovable and real her characters are. I felt their pain and yes, once again, this book made me cry like a baby. <br/><br/>If I could, I'd dive into this book and give all these characters a hug. I can't wait to re-read More than we can tell!<br/><br/><br/>Buddy RE-read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda' rel='nofollow noopener'>this queen</a> 🌠<br/>____<br/><u>First read</u> <i>2018</i><br/><br/>YA at its best. I gobbled this book up in one night, I just cou</span>
  <span id="freeText6155557199391291440" style="display:none"><u>Second Read</u> <br /><br />It was good the first time, it was brilliant the second time. <br /><br />Brigid Kemmerer amazes me everytime. I forgot how addictive her writing is and how lovable and real her characters are. I felt their pain and yes, once again, this book made me cry like a baby. <br /><br />If I could, I'd dive into this book and give all these characters a hug. I can't wait to re-read More than we can tell!<br /><br /><br />Buddy RE-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda" rel="nofollow noopener">this queen</a> 🌠<br />____<br /><u>First read</u> <i>2018</i><br /><br />YA at its best. I gobbled this book up in one night, I just couldn't get enough. Everything about this book was just perfection. And it really made me realize that you really have no idea what someone else is going through. <br /><br />This is a story about two broken people who help each other heal through a written correspondence. Juliet and Declan writing to one another about their grief brought me to tears quite a few times. It was awesome that they were there for one another without really knowing eachother. <br /><br />One aspect of the book I LOVed was Declan and Rev's friendship. I am a major fan of guy best friendships. Declan and Rev were no exception to that. They'd been best friends since kids and know everything about eachother, they're practically brothers. They're both outcasts with little to no experience with girls which I found refreshing and adorable. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘One who has unreliable friends may come to ruin, but there is a friend who sticks closer than a brother.’</b>
</i><br /><br />I'm going to start book 2 today and I have a feeling it's going to be just as great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6155557199391291440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8072886994829620021">*Price drop to $1.99 at Amazon US today, 8/1/18*<br/><br/><b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4629194.Brigid_Kemmerer' title='Brigid Kemmerer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brigid Kemmerer</a> does it again with a heartfelt, moving YA romance featuring a winning cast of characters. Get ready to feel things, folks!</b><br/><br/>I'm a huge <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4629194.Brigid_Kemmerer' title='Brigid Kemmerer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brigid Kemmerer</a> fan, and I talk about her books to anyone who will listen. Her <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/56771-elemental' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elemental Series</a> has not one but TWO books on my very exclusive all-time-favorites list, and I know what a true talent this author is. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30038855.Letters_to_the_Lost__Letters_to_the_Lost___1_' title='Letters to the Lost (Letters to the Lost, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Letters to the Lost</a> reminds me very much of a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575371.Katie_McGarry' title='Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katie McGarry</a> book in a good way. It is <b>ver</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8072886994829620021" style="display:none">*Price drop to $1.99 at Amazon US today, 8/1/18*<br /><br /><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4629194.Brigid_Kemmerer" title="Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Brigid Kemmerer</a> does it again with a heartfelt, moving YA romance featuring a winning cast of characters. Get ready to feel things, folks!</b><br /><br />I'm a huge <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4629194.Brigid_Kemmerer" title="Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Brigid Kemmerer</a> fan, and I talk about her books to anyone who will listen. Her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/56771-elemental" rel="nofollow noopener">Elemental Series</a> has not one but TWO books on my very exclusive all-time-favorites list, and I know what a true talent this author is. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30038855.Letters_to_the_Lost__Letters_to_the_Lost___1_" title="Letters to the Lost (Letters to the Lost, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Letters to the Lost</a> reminds me very much of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575371.Katie_McGarry" title="Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Katie McGarry</a> book in a good way. It is <b>very angsty</b> and a little depressing, but it never pushed me over my "heavy" limit. It did, however, make me want to hug the two MCs (and Rev, the best friend) very, very tightly. <br /><br />The best thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30038855.Letters_to_the_Lost__Letters_to_the_Lost___1_" title="Letters to the Lost (Letters to the Lost, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Letters to the Lost</a> is how <b>compulsively readable</b> it is. Brigid Kemmerer has a great sense of flow and pacing, and things never lagged, never grew dull. She kept everything swiftly moving, yet she really let the characters shine. The romance felt very organic and inevitable, which I always love. Though the book is YA (and the romance stays in strictly PG territory), the book never felt juvenile. It felt <i>real</i> and important, something that is often tricky to pull off. <br /><br />Sure, the concept isn't the most original in the world. I swear I've read a book with a similar plot-line, actually, but I couldn't place it. However, despite the fact that the story-line felt familiar, I thought it was an excellent read. And I CANNOT be any more excited for Rev's story. I mean, he practically stole the book, so a story from his POV would be divine. I think this is a series to watch. <br /><br />*Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review*</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6913022946309020118">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to Bloomsbury Publishing Plc (UK & ANZ) and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There is agony in that picture. Every time I look at it, I think, “I know exactly how she feels.””</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was a YA contemporary story, about two people brought together by grief.<br/><br/>Juliet was an interesting character, and it was clear that losing her mum had really destroyed her. I did think that the letter writing seemed to help her though, especially when Declan started writi</span>
  <span id="freeText6913022946309020118" style="display:none">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to Bloomsbury Publishing Plc (UK &amp; ANZ) and NetGalley.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There is agony in that picture. Every time I look at it, I think, “I know exactly how she feels.””</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This was a YA contemporary story, about two people brought together by grief.<br><br>Juliet was an interesting character, and it was clear that losing her mum had really destroyed her. I did think that the letter writing seemed to help her though, especially when Declan started writing back! Declan was another interesting character, if a little rough around the edges, and I really wanted to know more about why he had done what he had done to end up doing community service.<br><br>The storyline in this was about Juliet writing letters to her dead mother and leaving them at her grave, and Declan finding them and replying. At first Juliet was shocked, but once they started talking to each other over email, and realised that they both were hurting over losing someone, they seemed to start supporting each other, which was nice to see. There was a little bit of mystery to the story, and a couple of plot points which were a little easy to guess, but this was an enjoyable story overall. I wouldn’t call this a romance though, as we basically got no romance at all until the very, very end.<br><br>The ending to this was quite good, and I liked the way that things turned out for Juliet and Declan.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066772i/15045457.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>7 out of 10</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8911274828680281409"><i>5 Stars (Second Read 7/8/2018)<br/><br/>5 Stars (First Read 6/14/2017)</i><br/><br/>I'm a sucker for the secret admirer trope. Even though most of the time it's predictable, I always enjoy it and this was no exception. There were twists and turns I wasn't expecting, and the predictability of it wasn't really an issue because the author didn't keep the admirers a secret from the reader. I think that's the problem with some books of this trope, the author tries too hard and it becomes unrealistic, because how the hell co</span>
  <span id="freeText8911274828680281409" style="display:none"><i>5 Stars (Second Read 7/8/2018)<br><br>5 Stars (First Read 6/14/2017)</i><br><br>I'm a sucker for the secret admirer trope. Even though most of the time it's predictable, I always enjoy it and this was no exception. There were twists and turns I wasn't expecting, and the predictability of it wasn't really an issue because the author didn't keep the admirers a secret from the reader. I think that's the problem with some books of this trope, the author tries too hard and it becomes unrealistic, because how the hell could they both be so dense when so many clues are dropped? So the pacing in this one was perfect for me, and things were revealed exactly how I'd hoped they'd be.<br><br>Now because I suck and decided to wait three weeks before typing this up, this review is not going to be too detailed. Because if you know me you know that me trying to remember details (even about a book I love) past a few days, is about as successful as this baby trying to grab the spoon:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499104455ra/23191885.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, it ain't happening. What I <i>can</i> say is that I absolutely loved this! <i>This</i> is the reason I read YA. It's YA perfection. It's so much more than a romance, in fact they don't kiss <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[until the very end! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But I didn't mind, I was totally invested in them as people.<br><br>So if you like this trope and/or YA, I'd seriously consider this one :) It has a spin-off coming out next year and I can't wait!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499156962ra/23197629.gif" width="425" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And it wouldn't be one of my reviews if I didn't include some of my favorite quotes:<i>
  <blockquote>"I don't think it's depressing. I don't think it's hopeful, either. It's life. When everything goes to hell around you, the only way to go is forward."</blockquote>
</i><i>
  <blockquote>I can't force what I'm feeling to fit between chapters two and six in some handbook dealing with the death of a loved one.</blockquote>
</i><i>
  <blockquote>I don't know what the point of this story is, except maybe to say that sometimes you get to a point where it hurts too much, and you'll do anything to get rid of the pain.<br>Even if it means doing something that hurts someone else.</blockquote>
</i><i>
  <blockquote>Is there a way to show more of ourselves? Or are we all trapped in a single photograph that doesn't tell the whole story?</blockquote>
</i>Safety: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No OM/OW drama *I'm 96.72% sure <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Closure: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[As with most YA, the closure wasn't amazing. But I don't expect that with YA, I honestly think it'd be weird with a drawn out epilogue. I think the point is just to leave the reader feeling hopeful, and this did that for me. It ends with them sharing their first kiss. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2015614474" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015614474" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44125660-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600268807p2/44125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015614474?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/44125660-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44125660-beth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015614474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2343766573607640627"><b>4.5 STARS!</b><br/><i>Spoiler Free Review</i><br/><br/>Trigger Warning: Suicide, Alcoholism <br/><br/><i>”But 'never' is okay, too Jules. Never is always okay”</i> <br/><br/>This was not what I expected… not one little bit. I LOVED THIS! I’ve started to go into my books completely blind, if it’s something I want to read I try and avoid updates and all of that before actually reading it so I have zero expectations going in. Letters to the Lost is about a girl who is mourning her mother and she writes letters to her grave, a guy sees the letter and </span>
  <span id="freeText2343766573607640627" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS!</b><br /><i>Spoiler Free Review</i><br /><br />Trigger Warning: Suicide, Alcoholism <br /><br /><i>”But 'never' is okay, too Jules. Never is always okay”</i> <br /><br />This was not what I expected… not one little bit. I LOVED THIS! I’ve started to go into my books completely blind, if it’s something I want to read I try and avoid updates and all of that before actually reading it so I have zero expectations going in. Letters to the Lost is about a girl who is mourning her mother and she writes letters to her grave, a guy sees the letter and writes back, and that is where the whole story begins. We get two different POV in this and it was so well done because we see two different characters coming together over losses. <br /><br />A lesson I got out of this, is that you shouldn’t judge someone just by hear-say, there’s so much more what lies underneath and it really makes you think to not judge someone before you get to know and understand them. What was so compelling was learning the different backgrounds to the characters and it really did play on my heart strings.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br /><br /><b>Juliet</b> really did seem to get better and better as she started to realise certain things. She seems to want compare everyone to her mum, and I got the sense she put her dad down quite a bit, but as the story progressed you could see things clicking into place for her. She doesn’t always deal with things in the best positive way, but her development throughout was so well done!<br /><br /><i>Declan</i> should of just grabbed my heart and of said I won’t be needing it anymore. My heart seriously broke for him SO much. He has a reputation in the school and is going through community service, but he has had a shit hand dealt to him. He has to take on a lot of responsibility from a young age, a parent and step parent who seem to push him away, and no one really seems to believe in him. I loved the relationships he built and him forming trust with a select few who see there’s more to him. When he’s with Marisol my heart MELTS. I need more of Declan please.<br /><br />I was not expecting a character like <b>Rev</b>, my god. His backstory is so HEARTBREAKING, I want to just put him in my pocket and keep him forever. He is such a good friend to Declan and he wants to be there for him. It’s just so lovely, and to see him try and break out of his comfort zone, I CANNOT!<br /><br />What <b>I liked?</b><br />- It shows how other people deal with grief, we all deal with things differently and this book shows how you can handle things.<br />- THE LETTERS/EMAILS<br />- We got a reference to Humans of New York!<br />- An in depth description of what it’s like when someone takes a photo <br />- The friendships and relationships! It’s so hard to explain because there’s lots of little things going on in the background<br /><br />What I <b>didn’t like?</b><br />- Sometimes (at the beginning) Juliets' behaviour really annoyed me<br /><br />Overall I was pleasantly surprised, I didn’t expect the heartbreak, but the back stories of all of the characters was just so well done. I loved this so much more than what I thought I would.<br /><br />Letters to the Lost - 4.5 Stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2269096220?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">More than we can Tell</a> - 4 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="2343766573607640627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w4yQoDj0z0j1YmuYocF+ZwaRp5lOaBIrsf8alBjMTD5BWlEfPHJxCc1PICXljNmKE634zC2KTxtj/N7bguV/xg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZNa0UF62/i7h2x0tmYc/2yeZNB/B8Hr4kcxeUAk5b0LmAHXvWjBAb9n2VpDdypg2MqVrSqISJ8hDz5ofkxBcug==')})
  }

Or that she’s landed a job at the local tourist-trap museum. Or that she’s being heckled daily by the irritatingly hot museum security guard, Porter Roth—a.k.a. her new arch-nemesis. But life is whole lot messier than the movies, especially when Bailey discovers that tricky fine line between hate, love, and whatever-it-is she’s starting to feel for Porter.\n\nAnd as the summer months go by, Bailey must choose whether to cling to a dreamy online fantasy in Alex or take a risk on an imperfect reality with Porter. The choice is both simpler and more complicated than she realizes, because Porter Roth is hiding a secret of his own: Porter is Alex…Approximately.\n\nIn this delightfully charming teen spin on You’ve   <span id="freeText12573364409114697917" style="display:none">Brigid Kemmerer is the New York Times bestselling author of dark and alluring Young Adult novels like A Curse So Dark and Lonely, More Than We Can Tell, and Letters to the Lost (Bloomsbury), as well as paranormal YA stories like The Elemental Series and Thicker Than Water (Kensington). A full time writer, Brigid lives in the Baltimore area with her husband, her boys, her dog, and her cat. When she’s not writing or being a mommy, you can usually find her with her hands wrapped around a barbell. <br /><br /></span>
